يزيد عليها كل ما يقارنها فتكون مادة للمجموع متقدمة عليه في الوجودين ، ممتنعة الحمل عليه ضرورة لزوم اتحاد الموضوع والمحمول في الوجود، وقد تؤخذ لا بهذا الشرط بل مع تجويز أن يقارنها غيرها، وأن لا يقارنها وحينئذ إن كانت مبهمة محتملة للقولية على مختلفات الحقائق غير متحصلة بنفسها، بل بما ينضاف إليها، فتجعلها أحد تلك المختلفات فجنس، والمنضاف فصل، وإن كانت متحصلة بنفسها أو بما انضاف إليها فنوع فالحيوان بشرط أن لا يدخل فيه الناطق، مادة للإنسان جزء له غير محمول عليه، وبشرط أن يدخل نوع وهو الإنسان نفسه، ولا بشرط أحدهما جنس له محمول عليه - فلا يكون جزءاً له، وإنما يقال له الجزء لما يقع جزءاً من حده، ضرورة أنه لا بد للعقل من ملاحظته في تحصيل صورة الإنسان، وأما في الخارج فمتأخر، ضرورة أنه ما لم يوجد الإنسان لم يعقل له شيء يعمه وغيره. ما ذكرنا من معنى الماهية بشرط شيء وبشرط لا شيء ولا بشرط هو المشهور فيما بين المتأخرين وذكر ابن سينا أن الماهية قد تؤخذ لا شيء بأن يتصور معناه بشرط أن يكون ذلك المعنى وحده، ويكون كل بشرط ما يقارنه زائداً عليه، ولا يكون المعنى الأول مقولاً على ذلك المجموع حال المقارنة جزءاً منه مادة له، متقدماً عليه في الوجود الذهني والخارجي ضرورة امتناع تحقق الكل بدون الجزء ويمتنع حمله على المحمول لانتفاء شرط الحمل، وهو الاتحاد في الوجود، وقد يوجد لا بشرط أن يكون ذلك المعنى وحده، بل مع تجويز أن يقارنه غيره، وأن لا يقارنه. ويكون المعنى الأول مقولاً على المجموع حال المقارنة والمأخوذ على هذا الوجه، قد يكون غير متحصل بنفسه، بل يكون مبهماً محتملاً للمقولية على أشياء مختلفة الحقائق وإنما يتحصل بما ينضاف إليه، فيتخصص به ويصير هو بعينه أحد تلك الأشياء فيكون جنساً، والمنضاف الذي قومه وجعله أحد الأشياء المختلفة الحقائق فصلاً، وقد يكون متحصلاً بنفسه كما في الأنواع البسيطة، أو بما انضاف إليه فجعله أحد الأشياء، كما في الأنواع الداخلة تحت الجنس وهو نوع. مثلاً الحيوان إذا أخذ بشرط أن لا يكون معه شيء وإن اقترن به ناطق صار المجموع مركباً من الحيوان والناطق، ولا يقال إنه حيوان كان مادة، وإذا أخذ بشرط أن يكون معه الناطق متخصصاً أو متحصلاً به كان نوعاً، وإذا أخذ لا بشرط أن يكون معه شيء من حيث يحتمل أن يكون إنساناً أو فرساً، وإن تخصص بالناطق يحصل إنساناً، ويقال إنه حيوان كان جنساً. فالحيوان الأول جزء الإنسان متقدم عليه في الوجوديين. والثاني نفس الإنسان. والثالث جنس له محمول عليه فلا يكون جزءاً له لأن الجزء لا يحمل على الكل بالمواطأة لما مر وإنما يقال للجنس والفصل إنه جزء من النوع، لأن كلا منهما يقع جزءاً من حده ضرورة أنه لا بد للعقل من ملاحظتهما في تحصيل صورة النوع.
Everything that accompanies it adds to it, so it becomes matter for the composite, prior to it in both existences, impossible to predicate of it due to the necessity of the subject and predicate being identical in existence. And it may be taken not with this condition, but with the permission that something else may accompany it or not accompany it. At that time, if it is vague, potentially predicable of diverse realities, not determined by itself, but by what is added to it, then it makes it one of those diverse things, so it is a genus, and the added thing is a differentia. And if it is determined by itself or by what is added to it, then it is a species. So animal, taken with the condition that rational is not included in it, is matter for man, a part of him not predicated of him; and taken with the condition that rational enters, it is the species itself, namely man; and taken without either condition, it is a genus for him, predicated of him, so it is not a part of him. But it is called a part because it occurs as a part of his definition, necessarily because the mind must observe it in acquiring the form of man; whereas in the external it is posterior, necessarily because as long as man does not exist, nothing common to him and others is conceived. What we have mentioned of the meaning of quiddity with condition of something, with condition of nothing, and without condition is well-known among the later scholars. Ibn Sina mentioned that quiddity may be taken with no condition, i.e., its meaning is conceived with the condition that that meaning alone exists, and everything that accompanies it is additional to it. And the first meaning is not predicated of that composite at the time of accompaniment, being a part of it, matter for it, prior to it in mental and external existence due to the impossibility of the whole being realized without the part, and it is impossible to predicate it of the predicate because the condition of predication is absent, which is identity in existence. And it may exist without condition, i.e., that meaning alone exists, but with the permission that something else may accompany it or not accompany it. And the first meaning is predicated of the composite at the time of accompaniment. What is taken in this manner may be not determined by itself, rather it is vague, potentially predicable of things of diverse realities, and only becomes determined by what is added to it, so it becomes specialized by it and becomes itself one of those things, so it is a genus, and the added thing that strengthens it and makes it one of the diverse realities is a differentia. And it may be determined by itself, as in simple species, or by what is added to it making it one of the things, as in species falling under a genus, and it is a species. For example, animal: if taken with the condition that nothing is with it, even if rational is conjoined with it, the composite becomes composed of animal and rational, and it is not said that it is animal; it was matter. If taken with the condition that rational is with it, specialized or determined by it, it is a species. If taken without condition that something is with it, in terms of its possibility of being man or horse, and if specialized by rational, man results, and it is said that animal is a genus. So the first animal is part of man, prior to him in both existences; the second is man himself; the third is a genus for him, predicated of him, not a part of him, because the part is not predicated of the whole by synonymy, as previously mentioned. Rather, genus and differentia are said to be parts of the species because each occurs as a part of its definition, necessarily because the mind must observe them in acquiring the form of the species.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage defines the three modes of quiddity (mahiyya) and explains their logical roles in composition of genus, species, and differentia, following Ibn Sina. The author first explains the mode 'with condition of something' (bi-shart shay'): when quiddity is taken with the condition that something accompanies it, it becomes matter for the composite, prior to it in both mental and external existence, and cannot be predicated of the composite because the condition of predication (identity in existence) fails. Then the mode 'with condition of nothing' (bi-shart la shay'): the quiddity is taken alone, with nothing else; then whatever accompanies it is additional, and the quiddity is a part of the composite, not predicated of it. Finally, the mode 'without condition' (la bi-shart): the quiddity is taken without any condition, allowing for accompaniment or not; it is predicated of the composite. The author then applies these modes to the example of animal and man. Animal taken 'with condition that rational is not included' is matter for man, a part not predicated. Animal taken 'with condition that rational enters' is man himself, the species. Animal taken 'without condition' is a genus predicated of man, not a part. The author clarifies that genus and differentia are called 'parts' of the species only in definition, not in reality, because the mind needs them to conceive the species. The passage also mentions that Ibn Sina's classification is standard among later scholars.

Key Terms
ماهية (quiddity)
بشرط شيء (with condition of something)
بشرط لا شيء (with condition of nothing)
لا بشرط (without condition)
جنس (genus)
فصل (differentia)
نوع (species)
مادة (matter)
حمل (predication)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Genus and differentia are actual ontological parts of a species, like physical components.
Correction: Genus and differentia are only parts of the definition (logical parts); they are not separate entities in reality. The passage emphasizes that they are called 'parts' because the mind needs them to conceive the species, not because they exist as independent components.

Checkpoint
In the example of animal and man, which mode of taking 'animal' results in it being a genus predicated of man?
A) Animal taken with the condition that rational is excluded
B) Animal taken with the condition that rational is included
C) Animal taken without any condition
D) Animal taken as a simple species

Key Takeaway
The three modes of quiddity (bi-shart shay', bi-shart la shay', la bi-shart) determine whether a quiddity functions as matter, species, or genus in logical definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own core beliefs, are you treating them as quiddities taken 'with condition of nothing' (isolated and unapplied) or 'without condition' (open to relation with other truths)? Which mode leads to genuine understanding of your faith?
?
In your daily life, do you mistake the logical parts of your identity (like roles or labels) for your actual essence? How might the distinction between 'matter', 'species', and 'genus' help you see yourself more accurately before Allah?

Three Modes of Taking a Universal: Genus, Species, and Difference
Defines predication and explains the three conditions of universals with example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ways a universal can be taken—without condition, with condition of being alone, and with condition of something—and how these correspond to genus, species, and difference in logic.

Core Idea
A universal's role depends on how we consider it: alone, with something, or without condition.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid explains the logical concepts of genus, species, and difference by examining how a universal meaning is taken. It shows that the same term, like 'animal', can function differently depending on the condition attached. Before diving into the text, it's important to grasp that these distinctions are foundational for classification and definition in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the complete Arabic passage once without interruption to get the flow.
Notice the technical terms: jins, fasl, naw'.
2
Understand the definition of predication
The passage begins by defining predication as 'union in existence'. This is the basis for the rest.
This sets the stage for how universals relate to individuals.
3
Identify the three conditions
Look for the three ways a universal is taken: bi-shart an yakuna wahdahu (condition of being alone), bi-shart shay' (condition of something), and la bi-shart (without condition).
These correspond to material part, species, and genus.
4
Analyze the example of 'animal'
Follow how 'animal' taken with different conditions becomes a part, the species itself, or a genus.
The example clarifies the abstract concepts.
5
Learn the relationship between genus, species, and difference
The passage explains that genus and difference are parts of the species definition, and that genus is prior in intellect but posterior in external existence.
This resolves common misunderstandings about parts and wholes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمل، وهو الاتحاد في الوجود، وقد يوجد لا بشرط أن يكون ذلك المعنى وحده، بل مع تجويز أن يقارنه غيره، وأن لا يقارنه. ويكون المعنى الأول مقولاً على المجموع حال المقارنة والمأخوذ على هذا الوجه، قد يكون غير متحصل بنفسه، بل يكون مبهماً محتملاً للمقولية على أشياء مختلفة الحقائق وإنما يتحصل بما ينضاف إليه، فيتخصص به ويصير هو بعينه أحد تلك الأشياء فيكون جنساً، والمنضاف الذي قومه وجعله أحد الأشياء المختلفة الحقائق فصلاً، وقد يكون متحصلاً بنفسه كما في الأنواع البسيطة، أو بما انضاف إليه فجعله أحد الأشياء، كما في الأنواع الداخلة تحت الجنس وهو نوع. مثلاً الحيوان إذا أخذ بشرط أن لا يكون معه شيء وإن اقترن به ناطق صار المجموع مركباً من الحيوان والناطق، ولا يقال إنه حيوان كان مادة، وإذا أخذ بشرط أن يكون معه الناطق متخصصاً أو متحصلاً به كان نوعاً، وإذا أخذ بشرط أن يكون معه شيء بل من حيث يحتمل أن يكون إنساناً أو فرساً، وإن تخصص بالناطق يحصل إنساناً، ويقال إنه حيوان كان جنساً. فالحيوان الأول جزء الإنسان متقدم عليه في الوجوديين. والثاني نفس الانسان. والثالث جنس له محمول عليه فلا يكون جزءاً له لأن الجزء لا يحمل على الكل بالمواطأة لما مر وإنما يقال للجنس والفصل إنه جزء من النوع، لأن كلا منهما يقع جزءاً من حده ضرورة أنه لا بد للعقل من ملاحظتهما في تحصيل صورة مطابقة للنوع الداخل تحت الجنس، فبهذا الاعتبار يكون متقدماً على النوع في العقل بالطبع، وأما بحسب الخارج فيكون متأخراً، لأنه ما لم يوجد الإنسان مثلا في الخارج، لم يعقل له شيء يعمه وغيره، وشيء يخصه ويحصله ويصيره هو هو بعينه
Predication is union in existence. And it may exist without the condition that that meaning be alone, but rather with allowance that something else accompanies it or does not accompany it. The first meaning is predicated of the composite in the state of accompaniment. And the taken in this manner may be not determinate by itself, but rather vague, potential for predication on things of different realities, and it is only determined by what is adjoined to it, so it becomes specialized by it and becomes exactly one of those things, so it becomes a genus; and the adjoined which made it specific and made it one of the things of different realities is a difference. And it may be determinate by itself, as in simple species, or by what is adjoined to it making it one of the things, as in species that fall under a genus, and it is a species. For example, 'animal' when taken with the condition that nothing be with it, even if 'rational' is conjoined with it, the composite becomes a composition of animal and rational, and it is not said that it is animal; it was material. And when taken with the condition that 'rational' is with it, specialized or determined by it, it is a species. And when taken with the condition that something be with it, rather from the perspective that it can be human or horse, and if specialized by 'rational' it becomes human, and it is said that it is animal, it is a genus. So the first animal is a part of human, prior to it in the two existences. The second is the same as human. The third is a genus predicated of it, so it is not a part of it, because the part is not predicated of the whole by synonymity as has passed. Rather, genus and difference are said to be parts of the species, because each of them occurs as a part of its definition, necessarily because the intellect must observe them in obtaining a form matching the species that falls under the genus. So in this regard, it is prior to the species in the intellect by nature, but in terms of external existence it is posterior, because as long as human, for example, does not exist externally, nothing is conceived for it that encompasses it and other things, and something that particularizes it, determines it, and makes it exactly itself.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the modes of predication as they relate to universals. It begins by defining predication (al-haml) as union in existence. It then explains that a meaning (universal) can be taken in three ways: without condition (la bi-shart), with the condition that it be alone (bi-shart an yakuna wahdahu), or with the condition that something be with it (bi-shart shay'). The first mode (without condition) is the absolute universal. The author then describes how the universal may be non-determinate (mubham) or determinate (mutahassil). When taken without condition and non-determinate, it functions as a genus (jins) that is specified by an adjunct which becomes the difference (fasl). When determinate by itself or by adjunct, it is a species (naw'). The example of 'animal' (hayawan) and 'rational' (natiq) illustrates the three conditions: taken with the condition of being alone, animal is a material part; with the condition that rational is with it, animal is identical to the species human; with the condition that something (unspecified) is with it, animal is a genus. The passage then explains the logical relationships: the first animal is a part of human, prior in both mental and external existence (al-wujudiyayn); the second is the human itself; the third is a genus predicated of human, not a part because the part is not predicated of the whole by synonymity (bi al-muwata'ah). Genus and difference are parts of the species definition, and the genus is prior in intellect but posterior in external existence.

Key Terms
الحمل
بشرط أن يكون وحده
بشرط شيء
لا بشرط
جنس
فصل
نوع
مبهم
متحصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A universal term like 'animal' has a fixed logical role (always genus or always species).
Correction: The same term can function as a material part, a species, or a genus depending on the condition under which it is taken, as shown in the passage.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the three ways a universal can be taken?
A) Condition of alone, condition of something, without condition
B) Genus, species, difference
C) Simple, complex, vague
D) Rational, animal, human

Key Takeaway
A universal term like 'animal' can serve as a material part, a species, or a genus depending on the condition under which it is taken.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that a universal taken 'without condition' is vague and non-determinate. In your pursuit of Islamic knowledge, are there topics you approach with a 'no condition' mindset, allowing any interpretation to fit without seeking the precise conditions that make a concept determinate (like a species)? How would your understanding change if you insisted on identifying the difference (fasl) that makes each concept what it truly is?
?
The author states that genus is prior in intellect but posterior in existence. Have you ever believed you understood something (e.g., the nature of divine attributes) theoretically, only to find that your understanding was merely a 'genus'—vague and unspecific—until actual experience or deeper study gave it specificity? What is one area of your faith where you are content with a vague mental concept instead of pursuing the determinate species of true knowledge?
?
The difference (fasl) distinguishes one species from another within the same genus. In your own character, what is the 'difference' that distinguishes you from others who share your 'genus' (e.g., humanity, being a Muslim)? Are you actively defining that difference by your choices and actions, or are you leaving it unspecified and allowing circumstances to define it for you?

Clarifying 'Taken with the Condition of Being Alone'
Clarifies the intended meaning of the condition that the universal be alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meaning of the logical condition 'taken with the condition that it be alone' and how it differs from a literal reading.

Core Idea
The condition excludes inclusion in the definition, not accompaniment in existence.

This lesson addresses a common misunderstanding about a key logical term. The passage presents a critique and a clarification by Ibn Sina. We will see what the condition really means and why the literal reading leads to contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the critique and the clarification. Notice the two possible interpretations.
The passage is from a larger discussion about logical terms.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The literal reading: nothing accompanies it at all. The intended meaning: nothing else is included in its definition. Note the contradiction in the literal reading.
3
Analyze Ibn Sina's example
Ibn Sina defines 'body' as a substance with dimensions, with the condition that no other meaning (like sensation) is part of the definition. This shows the condition is about definitional inclusion, not existential accompaniment.
Example: body can still have sensation in reality, just not in its definition.
4
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding with the multiple-choice question. It directly checks the core idea of this lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيه مواضع بحث : ١ - أن المفهوم من المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده، هو أن لا يقارنه شيء أصلاً زائداً كان أو غير زائد وحينئذ يكون القول بكونه جزءاً أو منضماً إلى ما هو زائد عليه تناقضاً إلا أن المراد هو أن لا يدخل فيه غيره على ما صرح به أبو علي في بيانه حيث قال : أخذنا الجسم جوهراً ذا طول وعرض وعمق من جهة ما له هذا بشرط أنه ليس داخلاً فيه معنى غير هذا، بل بحيث لو انضم إليه معنى آخر من حس أو اغتداء كان خارجاً عنه
And in it there are points of discussion: 1. That the concept of the taken with the condition that it be alone is that nothing accompanies it at all, whether accidental or non-accidental. And then the statement that it is a part or adjunct to what is additional to it would be a contradiction, except that the intended meaning is that nothing else enters into it, as Abu Ali clarified in his explanation where he said: 'We took body as a substance having length, width, and depth, from the aspect that it has this, with the condition that no other meaning is inside it, rather such that if another meaning like sensation or nutrition is added to it, it would be external to it.'
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage presents the first of three points of critique regarding the earlier discussion. It concerns the interpretation of 'taken with the condition that it be alone' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart an yakuna wahdahu). The critique argues that if taken literally, this condition would mean that nothing whatsoever accompanies it, whether accidental (za'id) or non-accidental (ghayr za'id). If that were the case, then speaking of it as a part (juz') or as adjunct (mundamm) to something additional would be contradictory. However, the intended meaning, as clarified by Ibn Sina (Abu Ali) in his statement, is that nothing else is included in the definition of the term, not that it cannot be accompanied in existence. Ibn Sina's example of 'body' defined as a substance having length, width, and depth illustrates this: 'body' is defined with the condition that no other meaning like sensation or nutrition is part of its definition, but those can be added externally.

Key Terms
المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده
جزء
منضم
زائد
داخل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition 'taken with the condition that it be alone' means the thing cannot be accompanied by anything in existence.
Correction: It means that nothing else is included in its definition; accompaniment in existence is allowed.

Checkpoint
What is the correct interpretation of 'taken with the condition that it be alone' according to the critique?
A) Nothing accompanies it in existence
B) Nothing else is included in its definition
C) It is a simple concept
D) It cannot be a part of a composite

Key Takeaway
The condition 'taken with the condition that it be alone' means that nothing else is included in the definition, not that it cannot be accompanied in existence.

Inconsistency in Classifying the Non-Vague Universal
Points out inconsistency in classifying the non-vague universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in classifying the non-vague universal under two different conditions in Ibn Sina's system.

Core Idea
Classification must be consistent: the same universal cannot be both 'without condition' and 'with condition'.

This lesson examines a specific critique of Ibn Sina's classification of universals. The critic points out that placing the non-vague universal under two different categories creates a contradiction. Understanding this helps refine logical distinctions and highlights the need for precision in logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the two statements about the non-vague universal.
2
Identify the two classifications
The passage says the non-vague universal was first placed under 'taken without condition' and later described as 'taken with condition'. Spot these two claims.
3
Understand the contradiction
Realize that 'taken without condition' and 'taken with condition' are distinct categories. Placing the same item in both is inconsistent.
The basis is that 'taken without condition' is more general than 'taken with condition'.
4
Reflect on consistency
Consider why logical classifications must be internally consistent to be valid. This critique exposes a flaw that needs resolution.

Commentary
This is the second point of critique. It notes an inconsistency in the classification: the author (Ibn Sina) had placed the non-vague (ghayr al-mubham) universal under the division of 'taken without condition' (al-ma'khudh la bi-shart shay'), but later stated that it is 'taken with a condition' (ma'khudh bi-shart shay'). The basis for this contradiction is that the first (the non-vague without condition) is more general (a'amm) than the second (the non-vague with condition). Third Critique: Species as Composite of Genus and Difference
Sanusi critiques equating species with the conditioned universal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying species with the conditioned universal is a simplification and that species is actually the composite of genus and difference.

Core Idea
Species is not just the universal; it is the sum of genus and difference.

Sanusi critiques an imprecise definition of species. He argues that species is not merely the universal taken with a condition but the composite of genus and difference. This lesson unpacks that critique and clarifies the true logical nature of species.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to grasp Sanusi's point. Notice the technical terms.
2
Identify the concession
Sanusi calls the identification of species with 'the determined by adjunct' a 'tasamuh' (concession). Find this term and understand why it is a compromise.
The concession is based on the idea that genus, difference, and species are one in essence.
3
Understand the correction
Sanusi then states the correct view: the universal taken without condition, when considered in terms of its distinction from and union with what accompanies it, is essential.
This corrects the imprecise definition.
4
Reflect on the logical significance
Consider why precise definitions matter in logic. How does this critique affect the understanding of species?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣ - أن النوع هو مجموع الجنس والفصل فجعل عبارة عن المتحصل بما انضاف إليه والمأخوذ بشرط شيء تسامح، مبني على أن الجنس والفصل والنوع واحد بالذات. وحقيقة الكلام أن المأخوذ لا بشرط شيء إذا اعتبر : بحسب التغاير بينه وبين ما يقارنه من جهة والاتحاد من جهة كان ذاتياً
3. That the species is the sum of genus and difference, so making it an expression for the determinate by what is adjoined to it, and the taken with a condition, is a concession, based on the fact that the genus, difference, and species are one in essence. And the reality of the statement is that the taken without condition, when considered in terms of the distinction between it and what accompanies it from one aspect and the union from another aspect, is essential.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This is the third point of critique. It addresses the definition of species (naw'). The species is actually the sum (majmu') of genus (jins) and difference (fasl), so to equate the species simply with 'the determinate by adjunct' (al-mutahassil bi-ma indafa ilayhi) and 'the taken with a condition' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart shay') is a concession (tasamuh) — that is, an imprecise approximation. This concession is based on the claim that genus, difference, and species are one in essence (wahid bi al-dhat). The true reality is that the universal taken without condition (la bi-shart shay'), when considered from the aspect of its distinction (taghayur) from what accompanies it and from the aspect of its union (ittihad) with it, is essential (dhati). The critique thus highlights the need for precise definitions in logical analysis.

المأخوذ بشرط شيء

تغاير
اتحاد

Correction: Species is actually the composite (majmu') of genus and difference.

B) Because the species is simple
C) Because the adjunct is not essential
D) Because the genus is more general

Key Takeaway
Species is the sum of genus and difference, not merely the universal taken with a condition.

The Logical Priority of Genus and Species
Al-Taftazani states the correspondence and priority between genus and species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the genus is prior to the species in the intellect but posterior in external existence, and how this relates to the threefold division of meanings.

Core Idea
Genus precedes species in thought; species precedes genus in reality.

Sanusi begins by establishing the correspondence between genus and species, and their order of priority. Before diving into the details of the three logical divisions, we need to grasp this fundamental relation. This short passage sets the stage for the objections that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the basic claim about priority.
Notice the terms 'bi al-tab'' (by nature) and 'bi hasab al-kharij' (in external existence).
2
Identify the two types of priority
The passage distinguishes between priority in the intellect and priority in external existence. Find where each is mentioned and note the reasoning given.
3
Consider the example of human
The passage uses the example of a human to illustrate why the species is posterior externally. Try to think through the reasoning yourself.
Why can't we conceive of a universal that includes and specifies a human before a human exists externally?
4
Connect to the three divisions
This context prepares for the threefold division of meanings (taken with condition, etc.). Think about how the genus as 'matter' relates to these divisions.
The 'matter' here likely refers to the genus as a component of the species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطابقة للنوع الداخل تحت الجنس، فبهذا الاعتبار يكون متقدماً على النوع في العقل بالطبع، وأما بحسب الخارج فيكون متأخراً، لأنه ما لم يوجد الإنسان مثلا في الخارج، لم يعقل له شيء يعمه وغيره، وشيء يخصه ويحصله ويصيره هو هو بعينه، هذا ما ذكره أبو علي في الشفاء ولخصه المحقق في شرح الإشارات وفيه مواضع بحث:
١ - أن المفهوم من المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده، هو أن لا يقارنه شيء أصلاً زائداً كان أو غير زائد وحينئذ يكون القول بكونه جزءاً أو منضماً إلى ما هو زائد عليه تناقضاً إلا أن المراد هو أن لا يدخل فيه غيره على ما صرح به أبو علي في بيانه حيث قال: أخذنا الجسم جوهراً ذا طول وعرض وعمق من جهة ما له هذا بشرط أنه ليس داخلاً فيه معنى غير هذا، بل بحيث لو انضم إليه معنى آخر من حس أو اغتداء كان خارجاً عنه
٢ - أنه جعل غير المبهم من أقسام المأخوذ بلا شرط شيء وصرح آخراً بأنه مأخوذ بشرط شيء، ومبناه على ما مر من كون الأول أعم من الثاني.
٣ - أن النوع هو مجموع الجنس والفصل فجعل عبارة عن المتحصل بما انضاف إليه والمأخوذ بشرط شيء تسامح، مبني على أن الجنس والفصل والنوع واحد بالذات. وحقيقة الكلام أن المأخوذ لا بشرط شيء إذا اعتبر بحسب التغاير بينه وبين ما يقارنه من جهة والاتحاد من جهة كان ذاتياً محمولاً، وإذا اعتبر بحسب محض الاتحاد كان نوعاً، وهو المراد بالمأخوذ بشرط شيء
٤ - أنه كما أن الجنس يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأنواع، فكذلك النوع يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأصناف أو الأشخاص، فكيف جعل الأول مبهماً غير متحصل، والثاني متحصلاً غير مبهم؟ والجواب: أن العبرة عندهم بالماهيات والحقائق، فالمراد الإبهام وعدمه بالقياس إليها.
٥ - أن المادة إذا كانت من الأجزاء الخارجية، فمن أين يلزم تقدمها في الوجود العقلي؟ والجواب: أن ذلك من جهة أن تصور النوع يتوقف على تصور الجنس والفصل ومعروض الجنسية والجزئية واحد، هو الماهية الحيوانية، وإنما التغاير بحسب الاعتبار، حيث أخذت في الأول بشرط لا وفي الثاني لا بشرط.
وقد يقال: إن هذه المعاني إنما اعتبرت في الصور العقلية من المفهومات الكلية، فتكون المادة من المواد العقلية، وتقدمها بالوجود العقلي ضروري كتقدم المادة الخارجية بالوجود الخارجي، وأما التقدم بالوجود الخارجي فإنما هو بحسب المبدأ، فإن المواد العقلية مأخوذة من المبادىء الخارجية كالحيوان من البدن والناطق من النفس، فكما أن الحيوان المأخوذ مادة عقلية يتقدم الإنسان في الوجود العقلي كذلك، مبدؤه الذي هو البدن يتقدمه في الوجود الخارجي، حتى لو لم تكن المادة مأخوذة من مبدأ خارجي كاللون للسواد لم يكن له تقدم إلا في العقل، واعلم أن الحكيم المحقق مع مبالغته في أن المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده هو الجزء الموجود في الخارج، وأن المأخوذ لا بشرط شيء هو المحمول،
Corresponding to the species that falls under the genus; in this respect, it (the matter) is prior to the species in the intellect by nature, but in terms of external existence it is posterior, because as long as a human, for example, does not exist externally, nothing that includes him and others, nor something that specifies him and determines him and makes him precisely himself, is conceived. This is what Abu Ali mentioned in al-Shifa' and which the Muhaqqiq summarized in his commentary on al-Isharat. There are points of investigation in it:
1. That the concept of 'the taken with the condition that it alone exists' is that nothing accompanies it at all, whether additional or non-additional. Then to say that it is a part or joined to what is additional to it is a contradiction, except that the intended meaning is that nothing other than it enters into it, as Abu Ali stated in his explanation where he said: 'We took body as a substance possessing length, breadth, and depth, from the aspect that it has this, with the condition that no meaning other than this enters into it; rather, if another meaning of sense or nourishment were to join it, it would be external to it.'
2. That he made the non-ambiguous one of the divisions of 'the taken without condition' and later stated that it is 'taken with the condition of something'; this is based on what preceded that the first is more general than the second.
3. That the species is the sum of genus and differential, so to make it an expression for what has become determined by what has been joined to it and the 'taken with the condition of something' is a looseness, based on the fact that the genus, differential, and species are one in essence. The reality of the matter is that the 'taken without condition' when considered in terms of the distinction between it and what accompanies it in one respect and the union in another respect, it is an essential predicate; and when considered in terms of pure union, it is a species, and that is what is meant by 'taken with the condition of something'.
4. That just as the genus is likely to be one of the species, so too the species is likely to be one of the subcategories or individuals; so how can the first be made ambiguous and indeterminate while the second is determinate and not ambiguous? The answer: The criterion for them is the quiddities and realities, so ambiguity and non-ambiguity are intended in relation to them.
5. That if the matter is one of the external parts, whence does its priority in intellectual existence follow? The answer: That is because the conception of the species depends on the conception of the genus and differential, and the subject of genericity and particularity is one, namely the animal quiddity; rather, the distinction is by consideration, where in the first it is taken with the condition of not, and in the second without condition.
And it may be said: These meanings are considered only in the intellectual forms of universal concepts, so the matter is from the intellectual matters, and its priority in intellectual existence is necessary like the priority of external matter in external existence. As for priority in external existence, it is only in terms of the principle; for intellectual matters are taken from external principles, like animal from body and rational from soul. So just as animal taken as intellectual matter is prior to human in intellectual existence, likewise its principle which is the body is prior to it in external existence; if the matter were not taken from an external principle, like color for blackness, it would have no priority except in the intellect. Know that the wise Muhaqqiq, despite his insistence that 'the taken with the condition that it alone exists' is the existing part in the external, and that 'the taken without condition' is the predicate,
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a logical analysis and defense of the threefold division of meanings (makhudh) based on conditionality. The author first establishes the context: the genus (jins) corresponds to the species (naw') that falls under it, and in intellect (al-'aql bi al-tab') the genus is prior to the species, but in external existence the species is prior. He cites Avicenna and al-Tusi. Then he presents five objections (mawadi' bahth) and their answers.

1. The first point clarifies the meaning of 'taken with the condition that it alone exists' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart an yakuna wahdahu). This means that nothing accompanies it at all, whether additional (za'id) or not. The apparent contradiction (saying it is a part yet part implies something additional) is resolved by specifying that it means nothing extrinsic enters its definition, as Avicenna's example shows: 'body' as substance with dimensions, conditioned that no other meaning like sense or nourishment enters it.

2. The second point notes that the non-ambiguous (ghayr al-mubham) is classified under 'taken without condition' (al-ma'khudh la bi-shart shay'), but later it is said to be 'taken with the condition of something' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart shay'). This is built on the idea that the first (the taken without condition) is more general than the second (the taken with condition).

3. The third point addresses that species is normally the sum of genus and differential, so calling the species 'taken with condition of something' is loose (tasamuh). However, the underlying truth is that genus, differential, and species are one in essence (wahid bi al-dhat). When the taken without condition is considered in terms of distinction (taghayur) with what accompanies it, it is an essential predicate (dhati mahmul); when considered in terms of pure union (mahd al-ittihad), it is a species, which is what is meant by 'taken with condition of something'.

4. The fourth objection: if genus can be a species, and species can be a subcategory or individual, why is the first called ambiguous (mubham) and the second determinate (mutahassil)? Answer: the criterion is the quiddities (mahiyat) and realities; ambiguity or determinateness is in relation to them, not to lower levels.

5. The fifth objection: if matter is an external part, how can it be prior in intellectual existence? Answer: conception of species depends on conception of genus and differential; the subject of genericity and particularity is one (the animal quiddity). The distinction is by consideration: in the first (genus) it is taken with the condition of not (i.e., not being determined), in the second (species) it is taken without condition.

Finally, the passage adds that these meanings are considered in intellectual forms (suwar 'aqliyya) of universal concepts. The matter is intellectual matter, and its priority in intellectual existence is necessary, just as external matter is prior in external existence. The priority of intellectual matter in external existence is only according to the principle (mabda'). Example: animal (from body) and rational (from soul). If the matter is not taken from an external principle, like color for blackness, it has priority only in the intellect. The wise Muhaqqiq (al-Tusi) insists that 'taken with condition that it alone exists' is the part existing externally, and 'taken without condition' is the predicate.

Key Terms
الجنس
النوع
المادة
العقل بالطبع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think genus and species are equally abstract and have the same priority in both thought and existence.
Correction: The passage clarifies that genus is prior in the intellect but posterior in external existence. In thought, the more general is prior; in reality, the particular individual comes first.

Checkpoint

A) Prior
B) Posterior
C) Equal
D) Not mentioned

Key Takeaway
The genus is prior in the intellect because it is more general, but species are prior in external existence because individuals exist first.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a specific human being, not just a concept. Does your daily awareness of your own uniqueness humble you or make you feel self-important? How does knowing that Allah knows you as an individual, not merely as a type, change the way you approach your prayer today?
?
The genus is prior in thought, but the species is prior in reality. In your life, do you prioritize general principles over concrete actions? For example, do you spend more time learning about tawheed in theory than actually living it in specific situations? Which deserves more of your attention right now, and what is one specific step you can take to act on it?
?

What does it mean to you that Allah created you as a unique individual with a specific purpose? How should that shape your next decision, even a small one?

First Two Objections: The Meaning of Conditionality
Al-Taftazani presents and answers the first two objections regarding the definitions of the logical divisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two objections regarding the definition of 'taken with the condition that it alone exists' and the classification of the non-ambiguous term.

Core Idea
The condition 'that it alone exists' excludes only extrinsic meanings, not intrinsic parts.

After establishing the context, al-Taftazani presents five points of investigation. The first two objections clarify the precise meaning of 'taken with the condition that it alone exists' and address a seeming inconsistency in the classification of the non-ambiguous. These objections sharpen our understanding of the threefold division.

Guided Path
1
Read the first objection and answer
Read the Arabic for the first objection (numbered 1) and its resolution. Pay attention to the example of body given by Avicenna.
The objection is about a contradiction in the definition of 'taken with condition that it alone exists'.
2
Understand the resolution
The resolution specifies that the condition means no extrinsic meaning enters, not that it is completely isolated. The example of body with dimensions illustrates this.
3
Read the second objection and answer
Read the second objection (numbered 2) about the non-ambiguous being classified under 'taken without condition' but later called 'taken with condition of something'.
This is based on the generality of the first over the second.
4
Reflect on the logical distinction
Consider why the author considers these two points important for the overall theory of the three divisions.
They refine the definitions and prevent misinterpretation.

٤ - أنه كما أن الجنس يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأنواع، فكذلك النوع يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأصناف أو الأشخاص، فكيف جعل الأول مبهماً غير متحصل، والثاني متحصلاً غير مبهم؟ والجواب: أن العبرة عندهم بالماهيات والحقائق، فالمراد الإبهام وعدمه بالقياس إليها.
٥ - أن المادة إذا كانت من الأجزاء الخارجية، فمن أين يلزم تقدمها في الوجود العقلي؟ والجواب: أن ذلك من جهة أن تصور النوع يتوقف على تصور الجنس والفصل ومعروض الجنسية والجزئية واحد، هو الماهية الحيوانية، وإنما التغاير بحسب الاعتبار، حيث أخذت في الأول بشرط لا وفي الثاني لا بشرط.
وقد يقال: إن هذه المعاني إنما اعتبرت في الصور العقلية من المفهومات الكلية، فتكون المادة من المواد العقلية، وتقدمها بالوجود العقلي ضروري كتقدم المادة الخارجية بالوجود الخارجي، وأما التقدم بالوجود الخارجي فإنما هو بحسب المبدأ، فإن المواد العقلية مأخوذة من المبادىء الخارجية كالحيوان من البدن والناطق من النفس، فكما أن الحيوان المأخوذ مادة عقلية يتقدم الإنسان في الوجود العقلي كذلك، مبدؤه الذي هو البدن يتقدمه في الوجود الخارجي، حتى لو لم تكن المادة مأخوذة من مبدأ خارجي كاللون للسواد لم يكن له تقدم إلا في العقل، واعلم أن الحكيم المحقق مع مبالغته في أن المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده هو الجزء الموجود في الخارج، وأن المأخوذ لا بشرط شيء هو المحمول،
Corresponding to the species that falls under the genus; in this respect, it (the matter) is prior to the species in the intellect by nature, but in terms of external existence it is posterior, because as long as a human, for example, does not exist externally, nothing that includes him and others, nor something that specifies him and determines him and makes him precisely himself, is conceived. This is what Abu Ali mentioned in al-Shifa' and which the Muhaqqiq summarized in his commentary on al-Isharat. There are points of investigation in it:
1. That the concept of 'the taken with the condition that it alone exists' is that nothing accompanies it at all, whether additional or non-additional. Then to say that it is a part or joined to what is additional to it is a contradiction, except that the intended meaning is that nothing other than it enters into it, as Abu Ali stated in his explanation where he said: 'We took body as a substance possessing length, breadth, and depth, from the aspect that it has this, with the condition that no meaning other than this enters into it; rather, if another meaning of sense or nourishment were to join it, it would be external to it.'
2. That he made the non-ambiguous one of the divisions of 'the taken without condition' and later stated that it is 'taken with the condition of something'; this is based on what preceded that the first is more general than the second.
3. That the species is the sum of genus and differential, so to make it an expression for what has become determined by what has been joined to it and the 'taken with the condition of something' is a looseness, based on the fact that the genus, differential, and species are one in essence. The reality of the matter is that the 'taken without condition' when considered in terms of the distinction between it and what accompanies it in one respect and the union in another respect, it is an essential predicate; and when considered in terms of pure union, it is a species, and that is what is meant by 'taken with the condition of something'.
4. That just as the genus is likely to be one of the species, so too the species is likely to be one of the subcategories or individuals; so how can the first be made ambiguous and indeterminate while the second is determinate and not ambiguous? The answer: The criterion for them is the quiddities and realities, so ambiguity and non-ambiguity are intended in relation to them.
5. That if the matter is one of the external parts, whence does its priority in intellectual existence follow? The answer: That is because the conception of the species depends on the conception of the genus and differential, and the subject of genericity and particularity is one, namely the animal quiddity; rather, the distinction is by consideration, where in the first it is taken with the condition of not, and in the second without condition.
And it may be said: These meanings are considered only in the intellectual forms of universal concepts, so the matter is from the intellectual matters, and its priority in intellectual existence is necessary like the priority of external matter in external existence. As for priority in external existence, it is only in terms of the principle; for intellectual matters are taken from external principles, like animal from body and rational from soul. So just as animal taken as intellectual matter is prior to human in intellectual existence, likewise its principle which is the body is prior to it in external existence; if the matter were not taken from an external principle, like color for blackness, it would have no priority except in the intellect. Know that the wise Muhaqqiq, despite his insistence that 'the taken with the condition that it alone exists' is the existing part in the external, and that 'the taken without condition' is the predicate,
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a logical analysis and defense of the threefold division of meanings (makhudh) based on conditionality. The author first establishes the context: the genus (jins) corresponds to the species (naw') that falls under it, and in intellect (al-'aql bi al-tab') the genus is prior to the species, but in external existence the species is prior. He cites Avicenna and al-Tusi. Then he presents five objections (mawadi' bahth) and their answers.

1. The first point clarifies the meaning of 'taken with the condition that it alone exists' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart an yakuna wahdahu). This means that nothing accompanies it at all, whether additional (za'id) or not. The apparent contradiction (saying it is a part yet part implies something additional) is resolved by specifying that it means nothing extrinsic enters its definition, as Avicenna's example shows: 'body' as substance with dimensions, conditioned that no other meaning like sense or nourishment enters it.

2. The second point notes that the non-ambiguous (ghayr al-mubham) is classified under 'taken without condition' (al-ma'khudh la bi-shart shay'), but later it is said to be 'taken with the condition of something' (al-ma'khudh bi-shart shay'). This is built on the idea that the first (the taken without condition) is more general than the second (the taken with condition).

3. The third point addresses that species is normally the sum of genus and differential, so calling the species 'taken with condition of something' is loose (tasamuh). However, the underlying truth is that genus, differential, and species are one in essence (wahid bi al-dhat). When the taken without condition is considered in terms of distinction (taghayur) with what accompanies it, it is an essential predicate (dhati mahmul); when considered in terms of pure union (mahd al-ittihad), it is a species, which is what is meant by 'taken with condition of something'.

4. The fourth objection: if genus can be a species, and species can be a subcategory or individual, why is the first called ambiguous (mubham) and the second determinate (mutahassil)? Answer: the criterion is the quiddities (mahiyat) and realities; ambiguity or determinateness is in relation to them, not to lower levels.

5. The fifth objection: if matter is an external part, how can it be prior in intellectual existence? Answer: conception of species depends on conception of genus and differential; the subject of genericity and particularity is one (the animal quiddity). The distinction is by consideration: in the first (genus) it is taken with the condition of not (i.e., not being determined), in the second (species) it is taken without condition.

Finally, the passage adds that these meanings are considered in intellectual forms (suwar 'aqliyya) of universal concepts. The matter is intellectual matter, and its priority in intellectual existence is necessary, just as external matter is prior in external existence. The priority of intellectual matter in external existence is only according to the principle (mabda'). Example: animal (from body) and rational (from soul). If the matter is not taken from an external principle, like color for blackness, it has priority only in the intellect. The wise Muhaqqiq (al-Tusi) insists that 'taken with condition that it alone exists' is the part existing externally, and 'taken without condition' is the predicate.

Key Terms
المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده
المأخوذ بشرط شيء
المأخوذ لا بشرط
غير المبهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Avicenna's example, what is NOT allowed to enter into the definition of 'body' when taken with condition?
A) Length, breadth, depth
B) Sense or nourishment
C) Substance
D) Dimensions

Key Takeaway
The condition 'that it alone exists' only excludes extrinsic meanings, allowing the thing to still be a part of something else.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you define core beliefs in your faith, do you intentionally exclude extrinsic, non-essential meanings, or do you sometimes mix things up and create confusion? How can you apply the precision of these logical distinctions to protect your tawhid from false analogies?
?
The objection about the non-ambiguous shows that the same thing can be classified differently under different aspects. In your own understanding of Allah's attributes, are there places where you have unintentionally made two contradictory statements because you treated one aspect as the whole truth? What would it take to reconcile them with the help of clearer definitions?
?
Abu Ali's example of 'body' shows that a concept can be taken alone yet still be part of something greater. Are there Islamic concepts you treat as isolated, forgetting that they are meant to be integrated into a larger framework of iman? What practical change would you make to see them as parts of a whole?

Remaining Objections: Species as Sum of Genus and Differential
Al-Taftazani presents and answers the third through fifth objections and adds a concluding note on intellectual matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third, fourth, and fifth objections concerning the species, the ambiguity of genus, and the priority of matter, along with the final note on intellectual matter.

Core Idea
Species is the union of genus and differential; genus is ambiguous relative to quiddities, not individuals.

The final three objections delve deeper into the nature of species, the apparent symmetry between genus and species, and the priority of matter in intellectual existence. A concluding note explains how intellectual matter derives from external principles. These points complete the defense of the threefold division.

Guided Path
1
Read the third objection and answer
Read the third objection (numbered 3) about calling species 'taken with condition of something' being loose. Note the explanation that genus, differential, and species are one in essence.
This objection deals with the relationship between the logical sum and the divisions.
2
Read the fourth objection and answer
Read the fourth objection (numbered 4) about the asymmetry of ambiguity. The answer invokes quiddities and realities as the criterion.
3
Read the fifth objection and answer
Read the fifth objection (numbered 5) about the priority of matter if it is an external part. The answer depends on the subject being the quiddity and consideration.
4
Understand the final note
Read the concluding passage about intellectual matter and its priority. Note the examples of animal and body, rational and soul.
This ties the logical discussion to the broader metaphysical framework.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if genus can be a species, then the category 'genus' should be considered determinate, not ambiguous.
Correction: The passage explains that ambiguity is measured relative to quiddities, not to the fact that a genus can itself be a species of a higher genus.

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the fourth objection, what is the criterion for whether something is ambiguous or determinate?
A) Whether it can be a species of a higher genus
B) The quiddities and realities
C) The number of individuals under it
D) The external existence

Key Takeaway
The threefold division is defended by distinguishing considerations; species is a union of genus and differential considered under pure union, and matter's priority depends on whether it is intellectual or external.

Logic and Technical Terms

The Fourth Objection: Genus and Species Indeterminacy
Al-Taftazani presents and answers an objection about the indeterminacy of genus vs species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why genus is considered indeterminate relative to species and species determinate relative to genus, based on the criterion of quiddities.

Core Idea
Indeterminacy is relative to quiddities, not intrinsic.

Al-Taftazani presents a fourth objection to a previous distinction: if a species can be indeterminate like a genus, why treat them differently? The answer clarifies that the terms 'indeterminate' and 'determinate' are relative to quiddities (essences), resolving the apparent paradox.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection that compares genus and species: both can be one of many (species for genus, individuals for species). Note the challenge: why treat genus as indeterminate and species as determinate?
2
Identify the apparent paradox
Notice that the objector uses symmetry to argue inconsistency. The same logical property applies to both, so the distinction seems arbitrary.
3
Read the answer
Read the response: 'The criterion for them is the quiddities and realities, so the intended meaning of indeterminacy and its absence is with respect to them.'
Focus on the phrase 'with respect to them' (bi al-qiyasi ilayhā).
4
Understand the relativity
Understand that indeterminacy is relative. Genus is indeterminate relative to species, but species is determinate relative to genus. Yet a species can be indeterminate relative to its individuals. No absolute claim is made.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤ ـ أنه كما أن الجنس يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأنواع، فكذلك النوع يحتمل أن يكون أحد الأصناف أو الأشخاص، فكيف جعل الأول مبهماً غير متحصل، والثاني متحصلاً غير مبهم ؟ . والجواب : أن العبرة عندهم بالماهيات والحقائق، فالمراد الإبهام، وعدمه بالقياس إليها .
Fourth: That just as the genus can be one of the species, likewise the species can be one of the varieties or individuals, so how is the first made indeterminate and non-concrete, and the second concrete and non-indeterminate? The answer: The criterion for them is the quiddities and realities, so the intended [meaning] of indeterminacy and its absence is with respect to them.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection and its answer in a logical discussion. The objector notes that just as a genus can be one of its species, a species can be one of its varieties or individuals. So why is the first (genus) considered indeterminate and non-concrete, while the second (species) is considered concrete and not indeterminate? The answer explains that the criterion for them is the quiddities and realities. The intended meaning of indeterminacy or its absence is with respect to quiddities. So genus is indeterminate relative to species, but species is determinate relative to genus, yet a species may be indeterminate relative to its individuals. The answer resolves the paradox by clarifying the relative nature of these terms.

Key Terms
جنس (jins, genus)
نوع (naw', species)
مبهم (mubham, indeterminate)
متحصل (mutahassil, determinate)
ماهيات (mahiyyat, quiddities)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that genus is inherently indeterminate and species inherently determinate, independent of context.
Correction: The passage clarifies that these labels are relative to quiddities: genus is indeterminate when compared to its species, but species is determinate only in that same comparison; it may be indeterminate when compared to its individuals.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what determines whether something is indeterminate or determinate?
A) The number of instances
B) The quiddities and realities
C) The logical form
D) The matter

Key Takeaway
Genus and species are not absolutely indeterminate or determinate; their status depends on the quiddities by which they are measured.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you confidently labeled something or someone as 'good' or 'bad' without considering the perspective. How does this lesson's emphasis on relative indeterminacy challenge you to re-evaluate that judgment today?
?
When you hold a belief, do you treat it as absolutely 'determinate' while dismissing opposing views as 'indeterminate'? How can you apply the principle that determinacy is relative to quiddities to cultivate humility in your own understanding?
?
If the quiddities (realities) are the criterion, ask yourself: what is the ultimate reality (or quiddity) that determines truth in your life? Is it your own reasoning, cultural norms, or divine revelation? How does this lesson push you to align your judgments with that ultimate reality?

The Priority of Material Parts in Mental Existence
Al-Taftazani explains the logical priority of material parts in mental existence and responds to an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why material parts logically precede their composites in mental existence and how this relates to the distinction between genus and differentia.

Core Idea
Mental priority follows logical dependence, not temporal sequence.

In this passage, al-Taftazani addresses an objection regarding the priority of material (like genus) in mental existence. He clarifies that this priority is a logical priority tied to the dependence of the species concept on the genus and differentia. He also distinguishes between priority in the mind and priority in external existence, using analogies from body-soul and color-blackness. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection: if material (e.g., genus) is an external part, why does it have to precede in mental existence?
The objector questions the necessity of mental priority.
2
Follow the answer: logical dependence
The answer hinges on the fact that the concept of species depends on the concept of genus and differentia. The substrate is the same, but considered under different conditions.
Genus is taken 'bi-sharṭ lā' and species 'lā bi-sharṭ'.
3
Grasp the distinction between mental and external priority
Mental priority is necessary for mental forms, just as external priority is for external existence. However, external priority depends on the principle from which the mental material is taken.
Example: animal (mental material) from body (external principle).
4
Consider the counterexample of color and blackness
If the mental material is not taken from an external principle (like color for blackness), it has no priority except in the mind.
This reinforces that mental priority is not always mirrored externally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه - أن المادة إذا كانت من الأجزاء الخارجية، فمن أين يلزم تقدمها في الوجود العقلي؟ والجواب : أن ذلك من جهة أن تصور النوع يتوقف على تصور الجنس والفصل ومعروض الجنسية والجزئية واحد، هو الماهية الحيوانية، وإنما التغاير بحسب الاعتبار، حيث أخذت في الأول بشرط لا . وفي الثاني لا بشرط. وقد يقال : إن هذه المعاني إنما اعتبرت في الصور العقلية من المفهومات الكلية، فتكون المادة من المواد العقلية، وتقدمها بالوجود العقلي ضروري كتقدم المادة الخارجية بالوجود الخارجي، وأما التقدم بالوجود الخارجي فإنما هو بحسب المبدأ، فإن المواد العقلية مأخوذة من المبادىء الخارجية كالحيوان من البدن والناطق من النفس، فكما أن الحيوان المأخوذ مادة عقلية. يتقدم الإنسان في الوجود العقلي كذلك، مبدؤه الذي هو البدن يتقدمه في الوجود الخارجي، حتى لو لم تكن المادة مأخوذة من مبدأ خارجي كاللون للسواد لم يكن له تقدم إلا في العقل
Fifth: That if the material is from the external parts, then why does its priority in mental existence necessarily follow? The answer: That is because the concept of the species depends on the concept of the genus and differentia, and the substrate of genus-ness and particularity is one, which is the animal quiddity, and the difference is only according to consideration, where the first is taken with the condition of not [being with another], and the second unconditionally. And it may be said: These meanings are only considered in mental forms from universal concepts, so the material is from mental materials, and its priority in mental existence is necessary like the priority of external material in external existence. As for priority in external existence, it is only according to the principle: the mental materials are taken from external principles, like animal from body and rational from soul. So just as the animal taken as mental material precedes man in mental existence, similarly its principle, which is the body, precedes it in external existence, such that if the material were not taken from an external principle like color for blackness, it would have no priority except in the mind.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth objection and its answer. The objector asks: if the material is from external parts, why does it necessarily precede in mental existence? The answer: because the concept of the species depends on the concept of the genus and differentia. The substrate of genus-ness and particularity is one, namely the animal quiddity, but the difference is in consideration: in the first (genus) it is taken with the condition of not being with something else (bi-sharṭ lā), and in the second (species) it is taken unconditionally (lā bi-sharṭ). Then it is said: These meanings are considered in mental forms from universal concepts, so the material is from mental materials, and its priority in mental existence is necessary, like the priority of external material in external existence. As for priority in external existence, it is according to the principle: mental materials are taken from external principles, like animal from body and rational from soul. So just as the animal taken as mental material precedes man in mental existence, similarly its principle which is the body precedes it in external existence, such that if the material were not taken from an external principle like color for blackness, it would have no priority except in the mind.

Key Terms
مادة (madda, material)
جزء خارجي (juz' khariji, external part)
وجود عقلي (wujud 'aqli, mental existence)
جنس (jins, genus)
فصل (fasl, differentia)
بشرط لا (bi-sharṭ lā, conditioned by not)
لا بشرط (lā bi-sharṭ, unconditioned)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that priority in mental existence implies priority in external existence, or vice versa.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between mental priority (logical) and external priority (temporal or causal). They are not necessarily aligned; mental priority is about dependence in conception.

Checkpoint
What analogy is given to explain the priority of mental material?
A) Body and soul
B) Color and blackness
C) Both A and B
D) None

Key Takeaway
Material parts (like genus) have logical priority in mental existence, and this priority mirrors the external priority of their principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the priority of material in mental existence is necessary, like the priority of external material. But when you think about your own understanding of faith, do you sometimes confuse the logical order of concepts (like God's attributes) with temporal order? Ask yourself: In what area of your belief do you prioritize mental concepts over external reality, and how might that affect your worship?
?
The passage uses the example of 'animal from body and rational from soul' to illustrate how mental materials are derived from external principles. What external principles in your own life—people, experiences, texts—shape the mental concepts you hold about your religion? Have you ever mistaken a derived concept for the original? How can you ensure your mental constructs remain anchored to the external Revelation?
?
Al-Taftazani explains that difference lies in consideration (bi-sharṭ lā vs lā bi-sharṭ). Reflect on a time when you insisted on a certain condition or unconditionality in your understanding of a religious matter. Could it be that your perspective was merely a matter of consideration, not the essence? What would change if you adopted the opposite condition?

Al-Tusi's Contradiction in al-Tajrid
Al-Taftazani presents al-Tusi's known view and his contradictory statement in al-Tajrid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani identifies a contradiction between al-Tusi's established view on universals and what he wrote in al-Tajrid.

Core Idea
Even great scholars can contradict themselves, a fact al-Taftazani uses to question authorship.

Al-Taftazani begins by summarizing al-Tusi's known position on the part and the predicate, then points out that in al-Tajrid al-Tusi wrote something that contradicts his own principles. This discrepancy raises doubts about the authenticity of the work.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Tusi's known view
Al-Tusi insisted that what is taken with the condition of being alone is the part existing externally, and the unconditioned is the predicate not a part.
2
Read the accusation
Al-Taftazani claims that al-Tusi's statement in al-Tajrid is presented in a way that shows it is not from his works.
3
Connect to authorship debate
This contradiction is used as evidence that al-Tajrid may not be al-Tusi's own composition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن الحكيم المحقق (۱) [هو نصير الدين أبو جعفر محمد بن محمد الطوسي] مع مبالغته في أن المأخوذ بشرط أن يكون وحده هو الجزء (۲) [في (ب) الجوهر بدلاً من (الجزء)] الموجود في الخارج، وأن المأخوذ لا بشرط شيء هو المحمول، وليس بجزء أصلاً، وإنما يقال له جزء الماهية بالمجاز، لما أنه يشبه الجزء من جهة أن اللفظ الدال عليه يقع جزءاً من حدها، أورد هذا الكلام في كتاب التجريد (۱) [سبق التعريف بهذا الكتاب] على وجه يشهد بأنه ليس من تصانيفه وذلك أنه قال (۲) [سقط من (ب) لفظ (قال)] : قد تؤخذ الماهية محذوفاً عنها ما عداها بحيث لو انضم إليها شيء لكان زائداً عليها، ولا يكون هو (۳) [في (ب) هي بدلاً من (هو)] مقولاً على ذلك المجموع الحاصل منها، ومن الشيء المنضم إليها، والمأخوذ على هذا الوجه هو الماهية بشرط لا شيء، ولا توجد إلا في الأذهان وقد توجد الماهية لا بشرط شيء وهو كلي طبيعي موجود في الخارج، هو جزء من الأشخاص، وصادق على المجموع الحاصل منه، ومما انضاف إليه، وهذا خبط ظاهر وخلط لما ذكره في شرح الإشارات بما (٤) [في (ب) إنما بدلاً من (بما)] اشتهر بين المتأخرين وفيه شهادة صادقة بما رمى به ،التجريد من أنه ليس من تصانيفه جلالة قدره عن أن ينسب إلى غيره . مع
And know that the verifying philosopher [al-Tusi], despite his insistence that what is taken with the condition of being alone is the part existing in the external, and that what is taken unconditionally is the predicate and is not a part at all, but is called a part of the quiddity metaphorically because it resembles a part in that the word denoting it occurs as a part of its definition, he presented this statement in the book al-Tajrid in a manner that testifies that it is not from his works. For he said: The quiddity may be taken stripped of everything besides itself such that if something were joined to it, it would be additional to it, and it would not be predicated of that composite resulting from it and from the thing joined to it. That which is taken in this manner is the quiddity with the condition of nothing, and it does not exist except in minds. And the quiddity may exist unconditioned, and it is a natural universal existing in the external, it is a part of individuals, and it is true of the composite resulting from it and from what is added to it. And this is obvious error and confusion of what he mentioned in the Commentary on al-Isharat with what has become prevalent among later [scholars]. And in it there is a true testimony to the accusation that al-Tajrid is not from his works, [given] the loftiness of his rank from being attributed to others.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage contains a sharp criticism of a statement by al-Tusi (the 'verifying philosopher') in his book al-Tajrid. Al-Taftazani notes that despite al-Tusi's insistence that the part taken with the condition of being alone (bi-sharṭ an yakūna wahdahu) is the actual part existing in the external, and the unconditioned (lā bi-sharṭ shay') is the predicate and not a part at all but called a part of quiddity metaphorically, yet in al-Tajrid he wrote something that contradicts this. Al-Tusi said: 'The quiddity may be taken stripped of everything besides itself such that if something were joined to it, it would be additional to it, and it would not be predicated of the composite of it and that thing. That which is taken in this manner is the quiddity with the condition of nothing (bi-sharṭ lā shay'), and it does not exist except in minds. And the quiddity may exist unconditioned (lā bi-sharṭ shay'), which is a natural universal existing in the external, is a part of individuals, and is true of the composite of it and what is added to it.' Al-Taftazani calls this an obvious error and confusion, mixing what al-Tusi himself had stated in his commentary on al-Isharat with what has become known among later scholars. The passage ends by saying that this is a true testimony to the accusation that al-Tajrid is not from al-Tusi's own works, as he is too lofty to be attributed to others.

Key Terms
محقق (muḥaqqiq, verifier)
تجريد (Tajrid)
بشرط (bi-sharṭ, conditioned by)
لا بشرط (lā bi-sharṭ, unconditioned)
جزء (juz', part)
ماهية (māhiyya, quiddity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a scholar's works are always consistent.
Correction: Al-Taftazani shows that even al-Tusi can contradict himself, leading to questions about authorship.

Checkpoint
What does al-Taftazani claim about the statement in al-Tajrid?
A) It confirms al-Tusi's view.
B) It is presented in a way that shows it is not from al-Tusi's works.
C) It is a perfect summary.
D) It is a quote from Aristotle.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani uses the contradiction between al-Tusi's known view and his statement in al-Tajrid to question the authorship of al-Tajrid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The 'verifier' al-Tusi contradicted his own established view in another book. Are there beliefs or principles you hold that you have contradicted in your actions or statements? Will you take time today to identify such inconsistencies and resolve them?
?
If even a respected scholar like al-Tusi can have a work attributed to him that contradicts his known positions, how carefully do you verify the sources of your own knowledge? What step will you take this week to ensure your understanding of Islamic teachings comes from reliable, consistent sources?
?
Al-Taftazani used this contradiction to question authorship. Have you ever been too quick to accept a contradiction as a mistake rather than a sign of deeper error? How can you cultivate a critical yet fair approach when you encounter contradictions in what you read or hear?
